<div style="clear:both;"></div><div class="floatleft"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg" title="Signature"><img alt="Signature" data-file-height="954" data-file-width="1006" decoding="async" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg/100px-Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg/150px-Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg/200px-Jeanne_d%27Arc_signature_16_mars_1430.svg.png 2x" style="vertical-align: bottom" width="100"/></a></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Joan of Arc</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr"><b>Jeanne d'Arc</b></i> <small>pronounced¬†</small><span class="IPA" lang="fr-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ ían da Åk]</a></span>; <abbr title="circa">c.</abbr> 1412¬†‚Äì 30 May 1431) is a <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> of France, honored as a defender of the French nation for her role in the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Siege of Orl√©ans">siege of Orl√©ans</a> and her insistence on the <a href="/wiki/Coronation_of_the_French_monarch" title="Coronation of the French monarch">coronation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII of France</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a>. Stating that she was acting under divine guidance, she became a military leader who transcended gender roles and gained recognition as a savior of France.
</p><p>Joan was born to a propertied <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasant</a> family at <a href="/wiki/Domr%C3%A9my-la-Pucelle" title="Domr√©my-la-Pucelle">Domr√©my</a> in northeast France. In 1428, she requested to be taken to Charles, later testifying that she was guided by visions from the <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">archangel Michael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_the_Virgin" title="Margaret the Virgin">Saint Margaret</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="Catherine of Alexandria">Saint Catherine</a> to help him save France from English domination.
</p><p>Convinced of her devotion and purity, Charles sent Joan, who was about seventeen years old, to the siege of Orl√©ans as part of a relief army. She arrived at the city in April 1429, wielding her banner and bringing hope to the demoralized French army. Nine days after her arrival, the English abandoned the siege. Joan encouraged the French to aggressively pursue the English during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Loire_Campaign" title="Loire Campaign">Loire Campaign</a>, which culminated in another decisive victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Patay" title="Battle of Patay">Patay</a>, opening the way for the French army to advance on <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a> unopposed, where Charles was crowned as the King of France with Joan at his side. These victories boosted French morale, paving the way for their final triumph in the Hundred Years' War several decades later.
</p><p>After Charles's coronation, Joan participated in the unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Paris_(1429)" title="Siege of Paris (1429)">siege of Paris</a> in September 1429 and the failed <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_La_Charit%C3%A9" title="Siege of La Charit√©">siege of La Charit√©</a> in November. Her role in these defeats reduced the court's faith in her. In early 1430, Joan organized a company of volunteers to relieve <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Compi%C3%A8gne" title="Siege of Compi√®gne">Compi√®gne</a>, which had been besieged by the <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_(party)" title="Burgundian (party)">Burgundians</a>‚ÄîFrench allies of the English. She was captured by Burgundian troops on 23 May. After trying unsuccessfully to escape, she was handed to the English in November. She was put on trial by Bishop <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Cauchon" title="Pierre Cauchon">Pierre Cauchon</a> on accusations of <a href="/wiki/Heresy" title="Heresy">heresy</a>, which included <a href="/wiki/Blasphemy" title="Blasphemy">blaspheming</a> by wearing men's clothes, acting upon visions that were <a href="/wiki/Demon" title="Demon">demonic</a>, and refusing to submit her words and deeds to the judgment of the church. She was declared guilty and <a href="/wiki/Death_by_burning" title="Death by burning">burned at the stake</a> on 30 May 1431, aged about nineteen.
</p><p>In 1456, an inquisitorial court reinvestigated Joan's trial and overturned the verdict, declaring that it was tainted by deceit and procedural errors. Joan has been revered as a <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">martyr</a>, and viewed as an obedient daughter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, an early feminist, and a symbol of freedom and independence.  After the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, she became a national symbol of France. In 1920, Joan of Arc was <a href="/wiki/Canonization" title="Canonization">canonized</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> and, two years later, was declared one of the patron saints of France. She is portrayed in <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_Joan_of_Arc" title="Cultural depictions of Joan of Arc">numerous cultural works</a>, including literature, paintings, sculptures, and music.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Name_of_Joan_of_Arc" title="Name of Joan of Arc">Joan of Arc's name</a> was written in a variety of ways. There is no standard spelling of her name before the sixteenth century; her last name was usually written as "Darc" without an apostrophe, but there are variants such as "Tarc", "Dart" or "Day". Her father's name was written as "Tart" at her trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220‚Äì221]_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220‚Äì221]-4">[3]</a></sup> She was called "Jeanne d'Ay de Domr√©my" in Charles VII's 1429 letter granting her a coat of arms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage81_81]_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage81_81]-5">[4]</a></sup> Joan may never have heard herself called "Jeanne d'Arc". The first written record of her being called by this name is in 1455, 24 years after her death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220‚Äì221]_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220‚Äì221]-4">[3]</a></sup>
</p><p>She was not taught to read and write in her childhood,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_21]_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_21]-6">[5]</a></sup> and so dictated her letters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]-7">[6]</a></sup> She may have later learned to sign her name, as some of her letters are signed, and she may even have learned to read.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage268_268]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage247_247]_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage268_268]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage247_247]-8">[7]</a></sup> Joan referred to herself in the letters as <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">"Jeanne la Pucelle"</i></span> (Joan the Maiden) or as <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">"la Pucelle"</i></span> (the Maiden), emphasizing her virginity, and she signed "Jehanne". In the sixteenth century, she became known as the "Maid of Orleans".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]-7">[6]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_and_historical_background">Birth and historical background</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg"><img alt="A map of France, divided into various sections" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2038" data-file-width="1670" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg/220px-Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg/330px-Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg/440px-Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hundred_Years_War_1429_copy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>France, 1429<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpagen19_xviii]_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpagen19_xviii]-9">[8]</a></sup> <hr/> <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#ee6677; color:black;">¬†</span>¬†Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI of England</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#aa3377; color:white;">¬†</span>¬†Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Philip III of Burgundy</a></div> <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#4477aa; color:white;">¬†</span>¬†Controlled by <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII of France</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>Joan of Arc was born around 1412<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage55_55]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage278_278]_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage55_55]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage278_278]-10">[9]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Domr%C3%A9my-la-Pucelle" title="Domr√©my-la-Pucelle">Domr√©my</a>, a small village in the Meuse valley now in the <a href="/wiki/Vosges_(department)" title="Vosges (department)">Vosges department</a> in the north-east of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDLP2021Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDLP2021Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]-11">[10]</a></sup> Her date of birth is unknown and her statements about her age were vague.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage10_10]-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[b]</a></sup> Her parents were <a href="/wiki/Jacques_d%27Arc" title="Jacques d'Arc">Jacques d'Arc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Isabelle_Rom%C3%A9e" title="Isabelle Rom√©e">Isabelle Rom√©e</a>. Joan had three brothers and a sister.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page36_36]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage8_8]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT24_24]_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page36_36]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage8_8]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT24_24]-17">[15]</a></sup> Her father was a <a href="/wiki/Peasant" title="Peasant">peasant</a> farmer<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespagen15_1]_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespagen15_1]-18">[16]</a></sup> with about 50 acres (20¬†ha) of land,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage221_221]_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage221_221]-19">[17]</a></sup> and he supplemented the family income as a village official, collecting taxes and heading the local <a href="/wiki/Watchman_(law_enforcement)" title="Watchman (law enforcement)">watch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen33_19‚Äì20]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage221_221]_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen33_19‚Äì20]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage221_221]-20">[18]</a></sup>
</p><p>She was born during the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a> between England and France, that had begun in 1337<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage50_50]_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage50_50]-21">[19]</a></sup> over the status of English territories in France and <a href="/wiki/English_claims_to_the_French_throne" title="English claims to the French throne">English claims to the French throne</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage61_61]Perroy1959[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearswar0000perrpage69_69]_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage61_61]Perroy1959[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearswar0000perrpage69_69]-22">[20]</a></sup> Nearly all the fighting had taken place in France, devastating its economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage85_85‚Äì86]_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAberth2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfrombrinkofapoca0000aberpage85_85‚Äì86]-23">[21]</a></sup> At the time of Joan's birth, France was divided politically. The French king <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI_of_France" title="Charles VI of France">Charles VI</a> had recurring bouts of mental illness and was often unable to rule;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage143_143‚Äì144]_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage143_143‚Äì144]-24">[22]</a></sup> his brother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_of_Valois,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Louis of Valois, Duke of Orl√©ans">Louis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Duke of Orl√©ans">Duke of Orl√©ans</a>, and his cousin <a href="/wiki/John_the_Fearless" title="John the Fearless">John the Fearless</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Burgundy" title="Duke of Burgundy">Duke of Burgundy</a>, quarreled over the regency of France. In 1407, the Duke of Burgundy ordered the <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Louis_I,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Assassination of Louis I, Duke of Orl√©ans">assassination of the Duke of Orl√©ans</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage5_5]_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage5_5]-25">[23]</a></sup> precipitating a civil war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESeward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage144_144]_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESeward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage144_144]-26">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Duke_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Charles, Duke of Orl√©ans">Charles of Orl√©ans</a> succeeded his father as duke at the age of thirteen, and was placed in the custody of <a href="/wiki/Bernard_VII,_Count_of_Armagnac" title="Bernard VII, Count of Armagnac">Bernard, Count of Armagnac</a>; his supporters became known as <a href="/wiki/Armagnac_(party)" title="Armagnac (party)">"Armagnacs"</a>, while supporters of the Duke of Burgundy became known as <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_(party)" title="Burgundian (party)">"Burgundians"</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage5_5]_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage5_5]-25">[23]</a></sup> The future French king <a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII</a> had assumed the title of <a href="/wiki/Dauphin_of_France" title="Dauphin of France">Dauphin</a> (heir to the throne) after the deaths of his four older brothers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage168_168]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage21_21]_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage168_168]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage21_21]-27">[25]</a></sup> and was associated with the Armagnacs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage22_22],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage25_25]_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage22_22],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage25_25]-28">[26]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Henry_V_of_England" title="Henry V of England">Henry V of England</a> exploited France's internal divisions when he invaded in 1415.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page19_19‚Äì22]Tuchman1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailsdistantmirrorcal00tuchpage583_583‚Äì585]_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page19_19‚Äì22]Tuchman1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailsdistantmirrorcal00tuchpage583_583‚Äì585]-29">[27]</a></sup> The Burgundians took <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> in 1418.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESizer2007_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESizer2007-30">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage29_29]_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage29_29]-31">[29]</a></sup> In 1419, the Dauphin offered a truce to negotiate peace with the Duke of Burgundy, but the duke was <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_John_the_Fearless" title="Assassination of John the Fearless">assassinated by Charles's Armagnac partisans</a> during the negotiations. The new duke of Burgundy, <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Philip the Good</a>, allied with the English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage26_26‚Äì27]Burne1956[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtwarmili0000burnpage142_142]_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage26_26‚Äì27]Burne1956[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtwarmili0000burnpage142_142]-32">[30]</a></sup> Charles VI accused the Dauphin of murdering the Duke of Burgundy and declared him unfit to inherit the French throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage29_29]_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage29_29]-31">[29]</a></sup> During a period of illness, Charles's wife <a href="/wiki/Isabeau_of_Bavaria" title="Isabeau of Bavaria">Isabeau of Bavaria</a> stood in for him and signed the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Troyes" title="Treaty of Troyes">Treaty of Troyes</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGibbons1996[httpswwwjstororgstable3679229seq21_71]_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGibbons1996[httpswwwjstororgstable3679229seq21_71]-33">[31]</a></sup> which gave their daughter <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Valois" title="Catherine of Valois">Catherine of Valois</a> in marriage to Henry V, granted the succession of the French throne to their heirs, and effectively disinherited the Dauphin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage28_28‚Äì29]_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage28_28‚Äì29]-34">[32]</a></sup> This caused rumors that the Dauphin was not King Charles VI's son, but the offspring of an adulterous affair between Isabeau and the murdered duke of Orl√©ans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage189_189]_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage189_189]-35">[33]</a></sup> In 1422, Henry V and Charles VI died within two months of each other; the 9-month-old <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI_of_England" title="Henry VI of England">Henry VI of England</a> was the nominal heir of the <a href="/wiki/Dual_monarchy_of_England_and_France" title="Dual monarchy of England and France">Anglo-French dual monarchy</a> as agreed in the treaty, but the Dauphin also claimed the French throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECurryHoskinsRichardsonSpencer2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtcompani0000currpage105_105]_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECurryHoskinsRichardsonSpencer2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtcompani0000currpage105_105]-36">[34]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png"><img alt="Joan in dress facing left in profile, holding banner in her right hand and sheathed sword in her left." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="756" data-file-width="503" decoding="async" height="256" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png/170px-Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png/255px-Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png/340px-Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Contemporaine_afb_jeanne_d_arc.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Earliest extant representation of Joan of Arc,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage240_240‚Äì241]_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage240_240‚Äì241]-37">[35]</a></sup> drawing by Cl√©ment de Fauquembergue (May 1429, French National Archives)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[c]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In her youth, Joan did household chores, spun wool, helped her father in the fields and looked after their animals. Her mother provided Joan's religious education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage21_21]_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage21_21]-40">[37]</a></sup> Much of Domr√©my lay in the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bar" title="Duchy of Bar">Duchy of Bar</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen29_15]_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen29_15]-41">[38]</a></sup> whose precise feudal status was unclear;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page89_89]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen29_15‚Äì16]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage24_24‚Äì25]_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page89_89]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen29_15‚Äì16]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage24_24‚Äì25]-42">[39]</a></sup> though surrounded by pro-Burgundian lands, its people were loyal to the Armagnac cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage171_171]_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage171_171]-43">[40]</a></sup> By 1419, the war had affected the area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_20]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen35_21‚Äì22]_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_20]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen35_21‚Äì22]-44">[41]</a></sup> and in 1425, Domr√©my was attacked and cattle were stolen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_20]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage266_266]_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage20_20]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage266_266]-45">[42]</a></sup> This led to a sentiment among villagers that the English must be expelled from France to achieve peace. Joan had her first vision after this raid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen41_28‚Äì29]_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen41_28‚Äì29]-46">[43]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan later testified that when she was thirteen, around 1425, a figure she identified as <a href="/wiki/Michael_(archangel)" title="Michael (archangel)">Saint Michael</a> surrounded by angels appeared to her in the garden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage34_34‚Äì35]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage53_53‚Äì54]}Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT26_26]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT27_27]_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage34_34‚Äì35]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage53_53‚Äì54]}Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT26_26]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT27_27]-47">[44]</a></sup> After this vision, she said she wept because she wanted them to take her with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage22_22]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage22_22]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]-48">[45]</a></sup> Throughout her life, she had visions of St. Michael,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage58_58]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage88_88]_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage58_58]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage88_88]-49">[46]</a></sup> a patron saint of the Domr√©my area who was seen as a defender of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage18_18]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage132_132]_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage18_18]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage132_132]-50">[47]</a></sup>  She stated that she had these visions frequently and that she often had them when the church bells were rung.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage18_18]_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage18_18]-51">[48]</a></sup> Her visions also included St. Margaret and St. Catherine; although Joan never specified, they were probably <a href="/wiki/Margaret_the_Virgin" title="Margaret the Virgin">Margaret of Antioch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Alexandria" title="Catherine of Alexandria">Catherine of Alexandria</a>‚Äîthose most known in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage88_88‚Äì89]_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage113_113]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage88_88‚Äì89]-52">[49]</a></sup> Both were known as <a href="/wiki/Virgin_(title)" title="Virgin (title)">virgin saints</a> who strove against powerful enemies, were tortured and <a href="/wiki/Christian_martyr" title="Christian martyr">martyred</a> for their beliefs, and preserved their virtue to the death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Dworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage115_115‚Äì117]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage102_102‚Äì104]_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage26_26]Dworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage115_115‚Äì117]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage102_102‚Äì104]-53">[50]</a></sup> Joan testified that she swore a vow of virginity to these voices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Dworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage107_107]_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Dworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage107_107]-54">[51]</a></sup> When a young man from her village alleged that she had <a href="/wiki/Breach_of_promise" title="Breach of promise">broken a promise of marriage</a>, Joan stated that she had made him no promises,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage25_25‚Äì26]_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage25_25‚Äì26]-55">[52]</a></sup> and his case was dismissed by an ecclesiastical court.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage33_33]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage119_119]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen47_24]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage14_14]_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage33_33]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage119_119]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen47_24]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage14_14]-56">[53]</a></sup>
</p><p>During Joan's youth, a prophecy circulating in the French countryside, based on the visions of <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marie_Robine_of_Avignon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marie Robine of Avignon (page does not exist)">Marie Robine of Avignon</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">¬†[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marie_Robine" title="fr:Marie Robine">fr</a>]</span>, promised an armed virgin would come forth to save France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage64_64]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT34_34]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage25_25‚Äì26]_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage64_64]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT34_34]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage25_25‚Äì26]-57">[54]</a></sup> Another prophecy, attributed to <a href="/wiki/Merlin" title="Merlin">Merlin</a>, stated that a virgin carrying a banner would put an end to France's suffering.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage60_60]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage7_7]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage19_19]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage26_26]_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage60_60]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage7_7]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage19_19]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage26_26]-58">[55]</a></sup> Joan implied she was this promised maiden, reminding the people around her that there was a saying that France would be destroyed by a woman but would be restored by a virgin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page40Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage9_9]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage44_44]_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page40Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage9_9]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage44_44]-59">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[d]</a></sup> In May 1428,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage17_17]_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage17_17]-63">[59]</a></sup> she asked her uncle to take her to the nearby town of <a href="/wiki/Vaucouleurs" title="Vaucouleurs">Vaucouleurs</a>, where she petitioned the garrison commander, <a href="/wiki/Robert_de_Baudricourt" title="Robert de Baudricourt">Robert de Baudricourt</a>, for an armed escort to the Armagnac court at <a href="/wiki/Chinon" title="Chinon">Chinon</a>. Baudricourt harshly refused and sent her home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page40_40‚Äì41]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage56_56‚Äì57]_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page40_40‚Äì41]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage56_56‚Äì57]-64">[60]</a></sup> In July, Domr√©my was raided by Burgundian forces<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen47_33‚Äì34]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage16_16‚Äì17]_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen47_33‚Äì34]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage16_16‚Äì17]-65">[61]</a></sup> which set fire to the town, destroyed the crops, and forced Joan, her family and the other townspeople to flee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage103_103]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage26_26]_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage103_103]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage26_26]-66">[62]</a></sup> She returned to Vaucouleurs in January 1429. Her petition was refused again,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage34_34]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage18_18]_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage34_34]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage18_18]-67">[63]</a></sup> but by this time she had gained the support of two of Baudricourt's soldiers, <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Metz" title="Jean de Metz">Jean de Metz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertrand_de_Poulengy" title="Bertrand de Poulengy">Bertrand de Poulengy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage56_56],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage5668_68]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen56_42‚Äì43]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage88_88‚Äì90]_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage56_56],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage5668_68]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen56_42‚Äì43]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage88_88‚Äì90]-68">[64]</a></sup> Meanwhile, she was summoned to <a href="/wiki/Nancy,_France" title="Nancy, France">Nancy</a> under <a href="/wiki/Safe_conduct" title="Safe conduct">safe conduct</a> by <a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Duke_of_Lorraine" title="Charles II, Duke of Lorraine">Charles II, Duke of Lorraine</a>, who had heard about Joan during her stay at Vaucouleurs. The duke was ill and thought she might have supernatural powers that could cure him. She offered no cures, but reprimanded him for living with his mistress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage18_18‚Äì19]_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage18_18‚Äì19]-69">[65]</a></sup>
</p><p>Henry V's brothers, <a href="/wiki/John_of_Lancaster,_1st_Duke_of_Bedford" title="John of Lancaster, 1st Duke of Bedford">John of Lancaster, 1st Duke of Bedford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humphrey,_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Humphrey, Duke of Gloucester">Humphrey, Duke of Gloucester</a> had continued the English conquest of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page27_27‚Äì28]_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page27_27‚Äì28]-70">[66]</a></sup> Most of northern France, Paris, and parts of southwestern France were under Anglo-Burgundian control. The Burgundians controlled <a href="/wiki/Reims" title="Reims">Reims</a>, the traditional site for the coronation of French kings; Charles had not yet been <a href="/wiki/Coronation#Middle_Ages" title="Coronation">crowned</a>, and doing so at Reims would help legitimize his claim to the throne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage76_67]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage56_56]_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage76_67]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage56_56]-71">[67]</a></sup> In July 1428, the English had started to surround Orl√©ans, and had nearly isolated it from the rest of Charles's territory by capturing many of the smaller bridge towns on the <a href="/wiki/Loire" title="Loire">Loire</a> River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage97_97‚Äì98]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage97_97‚Äì98]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]-72">[68]</a></sup> Orl√©ans was strategically important as the last obstacle to an assault on the remainder of Charles's territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage10_10]_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage10_10]-73">[69]</a></sup> According to Joan's later testimony, it was around this period that her visions told her to leave Domr√©my to help the Dauphin Charles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage30_30]Goldstone2012[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmaidqueensecreth0000goldpage99_99‚Äì100]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage70_70]_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage30_30]Goldstone2012[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmaidqueensecreth0000goldpage99_99‚Äì100]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage70_70]-74">[70]</a></sup>
Baudricourt agreed to a third meeting with Joan in February 1429, around the time the English captured an Armagnac relief convoy at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Herrings" title="Battle of the Herrings">Battle of the Herrings</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Siege of Orl√©ans">Siege of Orl√©ans</a>. Their conversations,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen61_47]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage96_96‚Äì97]_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen61_47]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage96_96‚Äì97]-75">[71]</a></sup> along with Metz and Poulengy's support,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page89_89]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage36_36]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage20_20]_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page89_89]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage36_36]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage20_20]-76">[72]</a></sup> convinced Baudricourt to allow her to go to Chinon for an audience with the Dauphin. Joan traveled with an escort of six soldiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage36_36]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen62_48]_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage36_36]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen62_48]-77">[73]</a></sup> Before leaving, Joan put on men's clothes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage35_35]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage32_32‚Äì33]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage143_143‚Äì144]_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage35_35]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage32_32‚Äì33]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage143_143‚Äì144]-78">[74]</a></sup> which were provided by her escorts and the people of Vaucouleurs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen61_47]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage33_33]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage19_19‚Äì20]_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen61_47]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage33_33]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage19_19‚Äì20]-79">[75]</a></sup> She continued to wear men's clothes for the remainder of her life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_298]_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_298]-80">[76]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chinon">Chinon</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:KarlVII.jpg"><img alt="Miniature of Charles the seventh of France." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4025" data-file-width="3307" decoding="async" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/KarlVII.jpg/170px-KarlVII.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/KarlVII.jpg/255px-KarlVII.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/KarlVII.jpg/340px-KarlVII.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:KarlVII.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Charles_VII_of_France" title="Charles VII of France">Charles VII of France</a> by <a href="/wiki/Jean_Fouquet" title="Jean Fouquet">Jean Fouquet</a> (c. 1444, <a href="/wiki/Louvre" title="Louvre">Louvre</a>, Paris)</div></div></div>
<p>Charles VII met Joan for the first time at the Royal Court in Chinon in late February or early March 1429,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage46_46]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage22_22]_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage46_46]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage22_22]-81">[77]</a></sup> when she was seventeen<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT29_29]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage4_4]_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT29_29]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage4_4]-82">[78]</a></sup> and he was twenty-six.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage40_40]_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage40_40]-83">[79]</a></sup> She told him that she had come to raise the siege of Orl√©ans and to lead him to Reims for his coronation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page90_91]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage50_50]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen71_57]_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page90_91]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage50_50]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen71_57]-84">[80]</a></sup> They had a private exchange that made a strong impression on Charles; <a href="/wiki/Jean_Pasquerel" title="Jean Pasquerel">Jean Pasquerel</a>, Joan's confessor, later testified that Joan told him she had reassured the Dauphin that he was Charles VI's son and legitimate king.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page48_48]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage51_51]_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page48_48]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage51_51]-85">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Charles and his council needed more assurance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage53_53]_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage53_53]-86">[82]</a></sup> and sent Joan to <a href="/wiki/Poitiers" title="Poitiers">Poitiers</a> to be examined by a council of theologians, who declared that she was a good person and a good Catholic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page96_96]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage53_53]_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page96_96]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage53_53]-87">[83]</a></sup> They did not render a decision on the source of Joan's inspiration, but agreed that sending her to Orl√©ans could be useful to the king<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page50_50]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage34_34]_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page50_50]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage34_34]-88">[84]</a></sup> and would test if her inspiration was of divine origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage108_108]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage56_56]_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage108_108]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage56_56]-89">[85]</a></sup> Joan was then sent to Tours to be physically examined by women directed by Charles's mother-in-law <a href="/wiki/Yolande_of_Aragon" title="Yolande of Aragon">Yolande of Aragon</a>, who verified her virginity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage54_54]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage76_76]_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage54_54]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage76_76]-90">[86]</a></sup> This was to establish if she could indeed be the prophesied virgin savior of France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage107_107]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage55_55]_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage107_107]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage55_55]-91">[87]</a></sup> to show the purity of her devotion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage107_107]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage31_31]_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage107_107]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage31_31]-92">[88]</a></sup> and to ensure she had not consorted with the Devil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage55_55]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage138_138]_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage55_55]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage138_138]-93">[89]</a></sup>
</p><p>The dauphin, reassured by the results of these tests, commissioned <a href="/wiki/Plate_armour" title="Plate armour">plate armor</a> for her. She designed her own banner, and had a sword brought to her from under the altar in the church at <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Catherine-de-Fierbois" title="Sainte-Catherine-de-Fierbois">Sainte-Catherine-de-Fierbois</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page50_50‚Äì51]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage59_59‚Äì60]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage36_36‚Äì37]_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page50_50‚Äì51]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage59_59‚Äì60]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage36_36‚Äì37]-94">[90]</a></sup> Around this time she began calling herself "Joan the Maiden", emphasizing her virginity as a sign of her mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage220_220]-7">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>Before Joan's arrival at Chinon, the Armagnac strategic situation was bad but not hopeless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage54_54]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage54_54]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]-95">[91]</a></sup> The Armagnac forces were prepared to endure a prolonged siege at Orl√©ans,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage43_43‚Äì44]_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage43_43‚Äì44]-96">[92]</a></sup> the Burgundians had recently withdrawn from the siege due to disagreements about territory,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage108_108]_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage108_108]-97">[93]</a></sup> and the English were debating whether to continue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]-98">[94]</a></sup> Nonetheless, after almost a century of war, the Armagnacs were demoralized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page29_29]-99">[95]</a></sup> Once Joan joined the Dauphin's cause, her personality began to raise their spirits<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage39_39]_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage39_39]-100">[96]</a></sup> inspiring devotion and the hope of divine assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage103_103‚Äì104]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage31_31]_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage103_103‚Äì104]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage31_31]-101">[97]</a></sup> Her belief in the divine origin of her mission turned the longstanding Anglo-French conflict over inheritance into a religious war.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage55_55]-98">[94]</a></sup> Before beginning the journey to Orl√©ans, Joan dictated a letter to the Duke of Bedford warning him that she was sent by God to drive him out of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage78_78‚Äì79]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage34_34‚Äì35]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage34_34‚Äì35]_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage78_78‚Äì79]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage34_34‚Äì35]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage34_34‚Äì35]-102">[98]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_campaigns">Military campaigns</span></h2>
<h3><span id="Orl.C3.A9ans"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Orl√©ans">Orl√©ans</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg"><img alt="Joan of Arc on horseback with armor and holding banner being greeted by the people of Orl√©ans." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1060" data-file-width="802" decoding="async" height="291" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg/220px-Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg/330px-Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg/440px-Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scherrer_jeanne_enters_orlean.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Joan of Arc enters Orl√©ans</i> by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Scherrer" title="Jean-Jacques Scherrer">Jean-Jacques Scherrer</a> (1887, <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_des_Beaux-Arts_d%27Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts d'Orl√©ans">Mus√©e des Beaux-Arts d'Orl√©ans</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>In the last week of April 1429, Joan set out from <a href="/wiki/Blois" title="Blois">Blois</a> as part of an army carrying supplies for the relief of Orl√©ans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage110_110]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page71_71]_103-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage110_110]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page71_71]-103">[99]</a></sup> She arrived there on 29 April<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage114_114]_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage114_114]-104">[100]</a></sup> and met the commander <a href="/wiki/Jean_de_Dunois" title="Jean de Dunois">Jean de Dunois</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Legitimacy_(family_law)" title="Legitimacy (family law)">Bastard</a> of Orl√©ans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage50_50]_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage50_50]-105">[101]</a></sup> Orl√©ans was not completely cut off, and Dunois got her into the city, where she was greeted enthusiastically.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage114_114‚Äì115]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage72_72]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage40_40‚Äì41]_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage114_114‚Äì115]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage72_72]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage40_40‚Äì41]-106">[102]</a></sup> Joan was initially treated as a figurehead to raise morale,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage118_118]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage64_64]_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage118_118]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage64_64]-107">[103]</a></sup> flying her banner on the battlefield.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage168_168]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage114_114]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage68_68]_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage168_168]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage114_114]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage68_68]-108">[104]</a></sup> She was not given any formal command<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage39_39]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page76_76]_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERichey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage39_39]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page76_76]-109">[105]</a></sup> or included in military councils,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage71_71],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage75_75]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage39_39]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage64_64]_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage71_71],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage75_75]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage39_39]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage64_64]-110">[106]</a></sup> but quickly gained the support of the Armagnac troops. She always seemed to be present where the fighting was most intense, she frequently stayed with the front ranks, and she gave them a sense she was fighting for their salvation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage4_4]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage230_230]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage40_40]_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage4_4]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage230_230]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage40_40]-111">[107]</a></sup> Armagnac commanders would sometimes accept the advice she gave them, such as deciding what position to attack, when to continue an assault, and how to place artillery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page103_103‚Äì104]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage86_86]_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page103_103‚Äì104]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage86_86]-112">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 4 May, the Armagnacs went on the offensive, attacking the outlying <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">bastille de Saint-Loup</i></span> (fortress of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-de-Braye" title="Saint-Jean-de-Braye">Saint Loup</a>). Once Joan learned of the attack, she rode out with her banner to the site of the battle, a mile east of Orl√©ans. She arrived as the Armagnac soldiers were retreating after a failed assault. Her appearance rallied the soldiers, who attacked again and took the fortress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage116_116]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage74_74‚Äì75]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage43_43‚Äì44]_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage116_116]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage74_74‚Äì75]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage43_43‚Äì44]-113">[109]</a></sup> On 5 May, no combat occurred since it was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ascension_Thursday" title="Ascension Thursday">Ascension Thursday</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feast_day" title="Feast day">feast day</a>. She dictated another letter to the English warning them to leave France, and had it tied to a <a href="/wiki/Crossbow_bolt" title="Crossbow bolt">bolt</a> which was fired by a crossbowman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage150_150‚Äì151]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage57_57]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage43_44]_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage150_150‚Äì151]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage57_57]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage43_44]-114">[110]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Armagnacs resumed their offensive on 6 May, capturing <a href="/wiki/Saint-Jean-le-Blanc,_Loiret" title="Saint-Jean-le-Blanc, Loiret">Saint-Jean-le-Blanc</a>, which the English had deserted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage117_117]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45]_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage117_117]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45]-115">[111]</a></sup> The Armagnac commanders wanted to stop, but Joan encouraged them to launch an <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orl%C3%A9ans#Assault_on_the_Augustines" title="Siege of Orl√©ans">assault on <i>les Augustins</i></a>, an English fortress built around a monastery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage117_117]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage58_58]_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage117_117]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage58_58]-116">[112]</a></sup> After its capture,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage118_118]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page82_82‚Äì85]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45‚Äì46]_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage118_118]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page82_82‚Äì85]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage45_45‚Äì46]-117">[113]</a></sup> the Armagnac commanders wanted to consolidate their gains, but Joan again argued for continuing the offensive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page85_85]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage78_78]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage46_46]_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page85_85]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage78_78]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage46_46]-118">[114]</a></sup> On the morning of 7 May, the Armagnacs attacked the main English stronghold, <i>les Tourelles</i>. Joan was wounded by an arrow between the neck and shoulder while holding her banner in the trench on the south bank of the river, but later returned to encourage the final assault that took the fortress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage79_79‚Äì78]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage47_47]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage61_61]_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage79_79‚Äì78]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage47_47]Richey2003[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcwarrior0000richpage61_61]-119">[115]</a></sup> The English retreated from Orl√©ans on 8 May, ending the siege.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage119_119]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page91_91]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage81_81]_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage119_119]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page91_91]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage81_81]-120">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>At Chinon, Joan had declared that she was sent by God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage22_22]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage22_22]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]-121">[117]</a></sup> At Poitiers, when she was asked to show a sign demonstrating this claim, she replied that it would be given if she were brought to Orl√©ans. The lifting of the siege was interpreted by many people to be that sign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage56_56]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage56_56]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]-122">[118]</a></sup> Prominent clergy such as <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jacques_G%C3%A9lu&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jacques G√©lu (page does not exist)">Jacques G√©lu</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">¬†[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacques_G%C3%A9lu" title="fr:Jacques G√©lu">fr</a>]</span>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Embrun" title="Archbishop of Embrun">Archbishop of Embrun</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidul8dKmHXYt0CpgPA87_87]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidul8dKmHXYt0CpgPA88_88]_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidul8dKmHXYt0CpgPA87_87]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidul8dKmHXYt0CpgPA88_88]-123">[119]</a></sup> and the theologian <a href="/wiki/Jean_Gerson" title="Jean Gerson">Jean Gerson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMichelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage80_80‚Äì81]_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMichelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage80_80‚Äì81]-124">[120]</a></sup> wrote treatises in support of Joan after this victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELang1909[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmaidoffrancebein00languoftpage146_146‚Äì147]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELang1909[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmaidoffrancebein00languoftpage146_146‚Äì147]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage63_63]-125">[121]</a></sup> In contrast, the English saw the ability of this peasant girl to defeat their armies as proof she was possessed by the Devil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoyd1986[httpswwwjstororgstable20716744seq5_116]DeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage10_10]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage87_87]Seward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage213_213‚Äì214]_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoyd1986[httpswwwjstororgstable20716744seq5_116]DeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage10_10]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage87_87]Seward1982[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000sewapage213_213‚Äì214]-126">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loire_Campaign">Loire Campaign</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="infobox vcard" style="border-spacing:2px;"><tbody><tr><th class="infobox-above" colspan="2" style="font-size:125%; background-color:#C3D6EF;"><div class="fn" style="display:inline"><img alt="Coat of Arms of Jeanne d'Arc.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="331" decoding="async" height="24" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg/22px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg/33px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg/44px-Coat_of_Arms_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc.svg.png 2x" width="22"/> Joan of Arc</div></th></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em">Allegiance</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a></td></tr><tr><th class="infobox-label" scope="row" style="padding-right: 1em">Conflict</th><td class="infobox-data"><b><a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a></b></td></tr><tr><td class="infobox-full-data" colspan="2"><div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:237px">
<div class="center" style="font-weight:bold">Major battles and journeys</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1111531371">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output div.mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" data-graph-id="f6cfbe53e24e3fa939b19233323d375859805803" style="min-width:235px;min-height:160px"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="font-size:75%"><a class="mw-kartographer-maplink" data-lat="48" data-lon="2" data-mw="interface" data-overlays='["_95c1cb28f26c33809b7df75711f2db7475a25f24"]' data-style="osm-intl" data-zoom="6" href="/wiki/Special:Map/6/48/2/en">[Interactive fullscreen map]</a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:#000000 dashed 2px;">¬†</span>¬†Joan's journey to <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Chinon" title="Ch√¢teau de Chinon">Chinon</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#117733; color:white;">¬†</span>¬†<a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Siege of Orl√©ans">Orl√©ans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Loire_Campaign_(1429)" title="Loire Campaign (1429)">Loire Campaign</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-line mw-no-invert" style="display: inline-block; vertical-align: middle; width: 1.67em; height: 0; border-style: none; border-top: 2px dotted black;border-top:#332288 dashed 2px;">¬†</span>¬†<a href="/wiki/March_to_Reims" title="March to Reims">March to Reims</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#332288; color:white;">¬†</span>¬†Reims and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Paris_(1429)" title="Siege of Paris (1429)">Siege of Paris</a></div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#999933; color:black;">¬†</span>¬†Campaign against Perrinet Gressard</div><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#882255; color:white;">¬†</span>¬†<a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Compi%C3%A8gne" title="Siege of Compi√®gne">Compi√®gne</a></div></div>
</div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
