she should have been turned over to the appropriate authority, the bailiff of Rouen, for secular sentencing, but instead was delivered directly to the English<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage135_135]_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage135_135]-263">[258]</a></sup> and tied to a tall plastered pillar for <a href="/wiki/Death_by_burning" title="Death by burning">execution by burning</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage282_281‚Äì282]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage228_228‚Äì229]_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage282_281‚Äì282]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage228_228‚Äì229]-264">[259]</a></sup> She asked to view a cross as she died, and was given one an English soldier made from a stick, which she kissed and placed next to her chest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage222_223]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen359_341]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage238_238]_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage222_223]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen359_341]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage238_238]-265">[260]</a></sup> A processional <a href="/wiki/Crucifix" title="Crucifix">crucifix</a> was fetched from the church of Saint-Saveur. She embraced it before her hands were bound, and it was held before her eyes during her execution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage282_282‚Äì283]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage136_136]_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage282_282‚Äì283]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage136_136]-266">[261]</a></sup> After her death, her remains were thrown into the <a href="/wiki/Seine" title="Seine">Seine</a> River.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen359_341]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage137_137]_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage223_223]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen359_341]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage137_137]-267">[262]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aftermath_and_rehabilitation_trial">Aftermath and rehabilitation trial</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Rehabilitation_trial_of_Joan_of_Arc" title="Rehabilitation trial of Joan of Arc">Rehabilitation trial of Joan of Arc</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg"><img alt="A group of highly detailed and realistic painted plaster statues depicting four men wearing various ecclesiastical garments. They are arranged in a complex composition around a representation of Joan of Arc on a set of stairs." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3198" data-file-width="3484" decoding="async" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg/220px-Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg/330px-Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f0/Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg/440px-Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Monument_comm%C3%A9moratif_de_la_r%C3%A9habilitation_de_Jeanne_d%E2%80%99Arc.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Joan in the foreground, facing figures from her rehabilitation trial in the <i>Monument Commemorating the Rehabilitation of Joan of Arc</i>, a plaster work by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C3%89mile_Pinchon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="√âmile Pinchon (page does not exist)">√âmile Pinchon</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">¬†[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/%C3%89mile_Pinchon" title="fr:√âmile Pinchon">fr</a>]</span> (1909, <a href="/wiki/Noyon_Cathedral" title="Noyon Cathedral">Cath√©drale Notre-Dame de Noyon</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269">[f]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The military situation was not changed by Joan's execution. Her triumphs had raised Armagnac morale, and the English were not able to regain momentum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage57_57]CurryHoskinsRichardsonSpencer2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtcompani0000currpage106_106]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage496_496‚Äì497]_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage57_57]CurryHoskinsRichardsonSpencer2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtcompani0000currpage106_106]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage496_496‚Äì497]-270">[264]</a></sup> Charles remained king of France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage57_57]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage490_490]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage166_166]_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage57_57]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage490_490]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage166_166]-271">[265]</a></sup> despite a rival coronation held for the ten-year-old Henry VI of England at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Notre_Dame_de_Paris" title="Notre Dame de Paris">Notre-Dame cathedral</a> in Paris in 1431.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage229_229]_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage229_229]-272">[266]</a></sup> In 1435, the Burgundians signed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Arras_(1435)" title="Treaty of Arras (1435)">Treaty of Arras</a>, abandoning their alliance with England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage228_228]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page186_186]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage494_494]_273-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarker2009[httpsarchiveorgdetailsconquestenglishk0000barkpage228_228]DeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page186_186]Fuller1954[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmilitaryhistoryo01fullpage494_494]-273">[267]</a></sup> Twenty-two years after Joan's death, the war ended with a French victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castillon" title="Battle of Castillon">Battle of Castillon</a> in 1453,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage36_36]Burne1956[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtwarmili0000burnpage342_342]_274-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllmand1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailshundredyearsware0000allmpage36_36]Burne1956[httpsarchiveorgdetailsagincourtwarmili0000burnpage342_342]-274">[268]</a></sup> and the English were expelled from all of France except <a href="/wiki/Calais" title="Calais">Calais</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page230_230]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage231_231]_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page230_230]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage231_231]-275">[269]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan's execution created a political liability for Charles, implying that his consecration as the king of France had been achieved through the actions of a heretic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page224_224]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage230_230]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage313_313‚Äì314]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage62_62]_276-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page224_224]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage230_230]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage313_313‚Äì314]Vale1974[httpsarchiveorgdetailscharlesvii0000valepage62_62]-276">[270]</a></sup> On 15 February 1450, a few months after he regained Rouen, Charles ordered Guillaume Bouill√©, a theologian and <a href="/wiki/List_of_rectors_of_the_University_of_Paris" title="List of rectors of the University of Paris">former rector of the University of Paris</a>, to open an inquest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage3_3‚Äì4]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage189_189]_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage3_3‚Äì4]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage189_189]-277">[271]</a></sup> In a brief investigation, Bouill√© interviewed seven witnesses of Joan's trial and concluded that the judgment of Joan as a heretic was arbitrary. She had been a prisoner of war treated as a political prisoner, and was put to death without basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage230_230]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage149_149‚Äì155]_278-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage230_230]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage149_149‚Äì155]-278">[272]</a></sup>
Bouill√©'s report could not overturn the verdict but it opened the way for the later retrial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage121_121]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage18_318]_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage121_121]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage18_318]-279">[273]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1452, a second inquest into Joan's trial was opened by <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholic_Church)" title="Cardinal (Catholic Church)">Cardinal</a> <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_d%27Estouteville" title="Guillaume d'Estouteville">Guillaume d'Estouteville</a>, papal legate and relative of Charles, and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Br%C3%A9hal" title="Jean Br√©hal">Jean Br√©hal</a>, the recently-appointed Inquisitor of France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page228_228‚Äì229]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage151_151]_280-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page228_228‚Äì229]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage151_151]-280">[274]</a></sup> who interviewed about 20 witnesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page228_228‚Äì229]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage4_4]_281-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page228_228‚Äì229]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage4_4]-281">[275]</a></sup> The inquest was guided by 27 articles describing how Joan's trial had been biased.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage152_152‚Äì155]_282-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage152_152‚Äì155]-282">[276]</a></sup> Immediately after the inquest, d'Estouteville went to Orl√©ans on 9 June and granted an <a href="/wiki/Indulgence" title="Indulgence">indulgence</a> to those who participated in the ceremonies in Joan's honor on 8 May commemorating the lifting of the siege.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage34_34]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage34_34]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]-283">[277]</a></sup>
</p><p>For the next two years d'Estouteville and Br√©hal worked on the case.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122‚Äì123]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen368_350‚Äì351]Murray1902[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles5738957389-h57389-hhtmPage_372_372]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]_284-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122‚Äì123]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen368_350‚Äì351]Murray1902[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles5738957389-h57389-hhtmPage_372_372]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]-284">[278]</a></sup> Br√©hal forwarded a petition from Joan's mother, Isabelle, and Joan's two brothers Jean and Pierre, to <a href="/wiki/Pope_Nicholas_V" title="Pope Nicholas V">Pope Nicholas V</a> in 1454.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage264_264]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]_285-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage264_264]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]-285">[279]</a></sup> Br√©hal submitted a summary of his findings to theologians and lawyers in France and Italy,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_128]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen367_350]_286-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_128]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen367_350]-286">[280]</a></sup> as well as a professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Vienna" title="University of Vienna">University of Vienna</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage37_37]_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage37_37]-287">[281]</a></sup> most of whom gave opinions favorable to Joan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage235_235]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122]_288-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage235_235]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage122_122]-288">[282]</a></sup> After Nicholas V died in early 1455, the new pope <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Callixtus_III" title="Callixtus III">Callixtus III</a> gave permission for a rehabilitation trial, and appointed three commissioners to oversee the process: <a href="/wiki/Jean_Juv%C3%A9nal_des_Ursins" title="Jean Juv√©nal des Ursins">Jean Juv√©nal des Ursins</a>, archbishop of Reims; <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Chartier_(bishop)" title="Guillaume Chartier (bishop)">Guillaume Chartier</a>, bishop of Paris; and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Olivier_de_Longueil" title="Richard Olivier de Longueil">Richard Olivier de Longueil</a>, bishop of <a href="/wiki/Coutances" title="Coutances">Coutances</a>. They chose Br√©hal as Inquisitor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage124_124]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen369_351]Murray1902[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles5738957389-h57389-hhtmPage_373_373]_289-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage124_124]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen369_351]Murray1902[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles5738957389-h57389-hhtmPage_373_373]-289">[283]</a></sup>
</p><p>The rehabilitation trial began on 7 November 1455 at Notre Dame Cathedral when Joan's mother publicly delivered a formal request for her daughter's rehabilitation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage235_235]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen369_351]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage37_37]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]_290-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage235_235]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen369_351]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage37_37]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]-290">[284]</a></sup> and ended on 7 July 1456 at <a href="/wiki/Rouen_Cathedral" title="Rouen Cathedral">Rouen Cathedral</a>, having heard from about 115 witnesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage156_156]_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage156_156]-291">[285]</a></sup> The court found that the original trial was unjust and deceitful; Joan's abjuration, execution and their consequences were nullified.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage236_236]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen373_355]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage287_287‚Äì288]_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage236_236]Lowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen373_355]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage287_287‚Äì288]-292">[286]</a></sup> In his summary of the trial, Br√©hal suggested that Cauchon and the assessors who supported him might be guilty of malice and heresy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENapier2017[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidH2AuDwAAQBApgPT62_67]_293-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENapier2017[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidH2AuDwAAQBApgPT62_67]-293">[287]</a></sup> To emphasize the court's decision, a copy of the Articles of Accusation was formally torn up. The court ordered that a cross should be erected on the site of Joan's execution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page241_241]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage237_237]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage268_268]_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page241_241]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage237_237]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage268_268]-294">[288]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Visions">Visions</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jeanne_d%27_Arc_(Eugene_Thirion).jpg"><img alt="Joan seated and looking forward with her furled banner while an angel whispers in her ear. An armored figure with fleur-de-lys banner is blowing a horn in the background." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="907" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg/170px-Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg/255px-Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg/340px-Jeanne_d%27_Arc_%28Eugene_Thirion%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jeanne_d%27_Arc_(Eugene_Thirion).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Jeanne d'Arc √©coutant les voix</i> by Eug√®ne Thirion (1876, Notre Dame Church, Ville de Chatou)</div></div></div>
<p>Joan's visions played an important role in her condemnation, and her admission that she had returned to heeding them led to her execution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage217_217]Hobbins2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailstrialofjoanofarc00danipage24_24‚Äì25]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage33_33]_295-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage217_217]Hobbins2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailstrialofjoanofarc00danipage24_24‚Äì25]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage33_33]-295">[289]</a></sup> Theologians of the era believed that visions could have a supernatural source.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage13_13],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage27_27]_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage13_13],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage27_27]-296">[290]</a></sup> The assessors at her trial focused on determining the specific source of Joan's visions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage86_86]Weiskopf1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage127_127]_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage24_24]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage86_86]Weiskopf1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage127_127]-297">[291]</a></sup> using an ecclesiastical form of <span title="Limburgish-language text"><i lang="li">discretio spirituum</i></span> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Discernment_of_spirits" title="Discernment of spirits">discernment of spirits</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage32_32]_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage32_32]-298">[292]</a></sup> Because she was accused of heresy, they sought to show that her visions were false.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage29_29]_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage29_29]-299">[293]</a></sup> The rehabilitation trial nullified Joan's sentence, but did not declare her visions authentic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage236_236]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage140_140]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage236_236]Lightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage140_140]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage190_190]-300">[294]</a></sup>  In 1894, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_XIII" title="Pope Leo XIII">Pope Leo XIII</a> pronounced that Joan's mission was divinely inspired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage222_220‚Äì223]_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage222_220‚Äì223]-301">[295]</a></sup>
</p><p>Modern scholars have discussed possible neurological and psychiatric causes for her visions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage35_35‚Äì36]Henker1984[httpspubmedncbinlmnihgov6390693_abstract]Schildkrout2017[httpsajppsychiatryonlineorgdoi101176appiajp201717080948_¬ß6]_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage35_35‚Äì36]Henker1984[httpspubmedncbinlmnihgov6390693_abstract]Schildkrout2017[httpsajppsychiatryonlineorgdoi101176appiajp201717080948_¬ß6]-302">[296]</a></sup> Her visions have been described as hallucinations arising from <a href="/wiki/Epilepsy" title="Epilepsy">epilepsy</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEd'OrsiTinuper2006[httpswwwepilepsybehaviorcomarticleS1525-50500600175-2fulltext_abstract]Foote-SmithBayne1991[httpsonlinelibrarywileycomdoi101111j1528-11571991tb05537x_abstract]NicastroFabienne2016[httpswwwepilepsybehaviorcomarticleS1525-50501500698-8fulltext_abstract]_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEd'OrsiTinuper2006[httpswwwepilepsybehaviorcomarticleS1525-50500600175-2fulltext_abstract]Foote-SmithBayne1991[httpsonlinelibrarywileycomdoi101111j1528-11571991tb05537x_abstract]NicastroFabienne2016[httpswwwepilepsybehaviorcomarticleS1525-50501500698-8fulltext_abstract]-303">[297]</a></sup> or a temporal lobe <a href="/wiki/Tuberculoma" title="Tuberculoma">tuberculoma</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERatnasuriya1986[httpsjournalssagepubcomdoipdf101177014107688607900413_235]_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERatnasuriya1986[httpsjournalssagepubcomdoipdf101177014107688607900413_235]-304">[298]</a></sup> Others have implicated <a href="/wiki/Ergot#Effects_on_humans,_other_mammals_and_LSD" title="Ergot">ergot poisoning</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEShermanZimmerman2008[httpswwwtandfonlinecomdoiabs101300J053v02n03_08_abstract]_305-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEShermanZimmerman2008[httpswwwtandfonlinecomdoiabs101300J053v02n03_08_abstract]-305">[299]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Schizophrenia" title="Schizophrenia">schizophrenia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAllen1975[httpswebarchiveorgweb20131228212724httpswwwmedievalistsnetfiles09012321pdf_4‚Äì7]_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAllen1975[httpswebarchiveorgweb20131228212724httpswwwmedievalistsnetfiles09012321pdf_4‚Äì7]-306">[300]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delusional_disorder" title="Delusional disorder">delusional disorder</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMackowiak2007[httpsarchiveorgdetailspostmortemsolvin0000mackpage140_140]_307-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMackowiak2007[httpsarchiveorgdetailspostmortemsolvin0000mackpage140_140]-307">[301]</a></sup> or creative <a href="/wiki/Psychopathy" title="Psychopathy">psychopathy</a> induced by her early childhood rearing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHenderson1939_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHenderson1939-308">[302]</a></sup> One of the <a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_advocate" title="Devil's advocate">Promoters of the Faith</a> at her 1903 canonization trial argued that her visions may have been manifestations of <a href="/wiki/Hysteria" title="Hysteria">hysteria</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage220_220]_309-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage220_220]-309">[303]</a></sup> Other scholars argue that Joan created some of the visions' specific details in response to the demands of the interrogators at her trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHuizinga1959[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmenideashistoryt00huizpage223_223‚Äì224]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage104_104‚Äì105]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT37_37]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT38_38]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage130_130‚Äì131]_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHuizinga1959[httpsarchiveorgdetailsmenideashistoryt00huizpage223_223‚Äì224]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage104_104‚Äì105]Taylor2009[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT37_37]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidsV9kFj3O1noCpgPT38_38]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage130_130‚Äì131]-310">[304]</a></sup>
</p><p>Many of these explanations have been challenged;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[g]</a></sup> the trial records designed to demonstrate that Joan was guilty of heresy are unlikely to provide the objective descriptions of symptoms needed to support a medical diagnosis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEde_Toffol201681_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEde_Toffol201681-313">[306]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan's firm belief in the divinity of her visions strengthened her confidence, enabled her to trust herself,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page38_38‚Äì39]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage28_28]Henderson1939Schildkrout2017[httpsajppsychiatryonlineorgdoi101176appiajp201717080948_¬ß8]_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page38_38‚Äì39]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage28_28]Henderson1939Schildkrout2017[httpsajppsychiatryonlineorgdoi101176appiajp201717080948_¬ß8]-314">[307]</a></sup> and gave her hope during her capture and trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage140_140]_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage140_140]-315">[308]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Clothing">Clothing</span></h2>
<p>Joan's <a href="/wiki/Cross-dressing" title="Cross-dressing">cross-dressing</a> was the topic of five of the articles of accusation against her during the trial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarber1993[httpsarchiveorgdetailsvestedinterestsc00garbpage215_215]Schibanoff1996_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarber1993[httpsarchiveorgdetailsvestedinterestsc00garbpage215_215]Schibanoff1996-316">[309]</a></sup> In the view of the assessors, it was the emblem of her heresy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage117_117]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage31_31]_317-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage117_117]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage31_31]-317">[310]</a></sup> Her final condemnation began when she was found to have resumed wearing men's clothes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage217_217‚Äì218]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage132_132]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage31_31]Sullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage132_132]_318-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage217_217‚Äì218]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage132_132]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage31_31]Sullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage132_132]-318">[311]</a></sup> which was taken as a sign that she had relapsed into heresy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage38_38]_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage38_38]-319">[312]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="see caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue_Jeanne_Arc_place_Pyramides_Paris_4_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jeanne_d%27Arc_(Fr%C3%A9miet)" title="Jeanne d'Arc (Fr√©miet)"><i>Jeanne d'Arc</i></a>, a gilded bronze statue by <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Fr%C3%A9miet" title="Emmanuel Fr√©miet">Emmanuel Fr√©miet</a> (1874, <a href="/wiki/Place_des_Pyramides" title="Place des Pyramides">Place des Pyramides</a></div></div></div>
<p>From the time of her journey to Chinon to her abjuration, Joan usually wore men's clothes<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane2002[httpsarchiveorgdetailsperformanceofsel0000cranpage74_74]Fraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage28_28,_fn18]_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane2002[httpsarchiveorgdetailsperformanceofsel0000cranpage74_74]Fraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage28_28,_fn18]-320">[313]</a></sup> and cropped her hair in a male fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_307]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage42_42]_321-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_307]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage42_42]-321">[314]</a></sup> When she left Vaucouleurs to see the Dauphin in Chinon, Joan was said to have worn a black <a href="/wiki/Doublet_(clothing)" title="Doublet (clothing)">doublet</a>, a black tunic, and a short black cap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_307]_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_307]-322">[315]</a></sup> By the time she was captured, she had acquired more elaborate outfits. At her trial, she was accused of wearing <a href="/wiki/Breeches" title="Breeches">breeches</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Mantle_(clothing)" title="Mantle (clothing)">mantle</a>, a coat of <a href="/wiki/Chain_mail" title="Chain mail">mail</a>, a doublet, hose joined to the doublet with twenty laces, tight boots, spurs, a <a href="/wiki/Breastplate" title="Breastplate">breastplate</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buskins" title="Buskins">buskins</a>, a sword, a dagger, and a lance. She was also described as wearing furs, a golden <a href="/wiki/Surcoat" title="Surcoat">surcoat</a> over her armor, and sumptuous <a href="/wiki/Riding_habit" title="Riding habit">riding habits</a> made of precious cloth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage192_192]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage34_34]_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage192_192]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage34_34]-323">[316]</a></sup>
</p><p>During the trial proceedings, Joan is not recorded as giving a practical reason why she cross-dressed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA67_67]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage144_144]_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA67_67]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage144_144]-324">[317]</a></sup> She stated that it was her own choice to wear men's clothes,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage35_35‚Äì37]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage91_91‚Äì92]_325-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage35_35‚Äì37]Sackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage91_91‚Äì92]-325">[318]</a></sup> and that she did so not at the request of men but by the command of God and his angels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_298]Garber1993[httpsarchiveorgdetailsvestedinterestsc00garbpage216_216]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage32_32‚Äì33]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage144_144‚Äì146]_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_298]Garber1993[httpsarchiveorgdetailsvestedinterestsc00garbpage216_216]Lucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage32_32‚Äì33]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage144_144‚Äì146]-326">[319]</a></sup> She stated she would return to wearing women's clothes when she fulfilled her calling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan2011[httpswwwjstororgstable23347178_316]_327-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan2011[httpswwwjstororgstable23347178_316]-327">[320]</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Joan's cross-dressing was used to justify her execution, the church's position on it was not clear. In general, it was seen as a sin, but there was no agreement about its severity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA61_61]_328-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA61_61]-328">[321]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Aquinas" title="Thomas Aquinas">Thomas Aquinas</a> stated that a woman may wear a man's clothes to hide herself from enemies or if no other clothes were available,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage43_42]_329-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage43_42]-329">[322]</a></sup> and Joan did both, wearing them in enemy territory to get to Chinon,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage92_92‚Äì93]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage41_41]_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESackville-West1936[httpsarchiveorgdetailssaintjoanofarcbo0000sackpage92_92‚Äì93]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage41_41]-330">[323]</a></sup> and in her prison cell after her abjuration when her dress was taken from her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage132_132]_331-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA66_66]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage132_132]-331">[324]</a></sup> Soon after the siege of Orl√©ans was lifted, Jean Gerson said that Joan's male clothes and haircut were appropriate for her calling, as she was a warrior and men's clothes were more practical.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_301]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage184_184]_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_301]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage184_184]-332">[325]</a></sup>
</p><p>Cross-dressing may have helped her maintain her virginity by deterring rape<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage125_125‚Äì126]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage216_216]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage251_251‚Äì252]Hotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA67_67]_333-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage125_125‚Äì126]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage216_216]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage251_251‚Äì252]Hotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA67_67]-333">[326]</a></sup> and signaling her unavailability as a sexual object;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage126_126]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage52_52]_334-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage126_126]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage52_52]-334">[327]</a></sup> scholars have stated that when she was imprisoned, wearing men's clothes would have only been a minor deterrent to rape as she was shackled most of the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA64_64‚Äì65]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage58_58]_335-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHotchkiss2000[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidfrPPPIJvUDgCpgPA64_64‚Äì65]Schibanoff1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage58_58]-335">[328]</a></sup> For most of her active life, Joan did not cross-dress to hide her gender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBullough1974Crane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_310]Sproles1996[httpswwwjstororgstable23539706_163]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage147_147]_336-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBullough1974Crane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_310]Sproles1996[httpswwwjstororgstable23539706_163]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage147_147]-336">[329]</a></sup> Rather, it may have functioned to emphasize her unique identity<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane2002[httpsarchiveorgdetailsperformanceofsel0000cranpage78_78]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage142_142]_337-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane2002[httpsarchiveorgdetailsperformanceofsel0000cranpage78_78]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage142_142]-337">[330]</a></sup> as <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">La Pucelle</i></span>, a model of virtue that transcends <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gender_roles" title="Gender roles">gender roles</a> and inspires people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_305‚Äì306]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage146_146‚Äì147]_338-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECrane1996[httpswebarchiveorgweb20160705094811httpsfacultysmuedubwheelerjoan_of_arcolr08_clothingjoanofarc_cranepdf_305‚Äì306]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage146_146‚Äì147]-338">[331]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<p>Joan is one of the most studied people of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepagen19_3]_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepagen19_3]-339">[332]</a></sup> partly because her two trials provided a wealth of documents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage16_16‚Äì17]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage6_4‚Äì6]_340-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage16_16‚Äì17]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage6_4‚Äì6]-340">[333]</a></sup> Her image, changing over time, has included being the savior of France, an obedient daughter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, an early feminist, and a symbol of freedom and independence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESexsmith1990[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458_125],_[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458seq5_129]_341-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESexsmith1990[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458_125],_[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458seq5_129]-341">[334]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_leader_and_symbol_of_France">Military leader and symbol of France</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Joan of Arc on horseback, with sword in right hand" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4303" data-file-width="3702" decoding="async" height="198" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Statue_of_Jeanne_d%27Arc_in_Orl%C3%A9ans_A_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Joan of Arc</i>, statue by <a href="/wiki/Denis_Foyatier" title="Denis Foyatier">Denis Foyatier</a> (1855, <a href="/wiki/Orl%C3%A9ans" title="Orl√©ans">Orl√©ans</a>)</div></div></div>
<p>Joan's reputation as a military leader who helped drive the English from France began to form before her death. Just after Charles's coronation, <a href="/wiki/Christine_de_Pizan" title="Christine de Pizan">Christine de Pizan</a> wrote the poem <i>Diti√© de Jehanne D'Arc</i>, celebrating Joan as a supporter of Charles sent by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divine_Providence" title="Divine Providence">Divine Providence</a>; the poem captured the "surge of optimism" and "sense of wonder and gratitude" that "swept through the whole of the French" after the triumph at Orl√©ans, according to Kennedy and Varty (1977).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKennedyVarty1977[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidqogHAQAAIAAJpgPA1_1]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage25_25]_342-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKennedyVarty1977[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidqogHAQAAIAAJpgPA1_1]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage25_25]-342">[335]</a></sup> As early as 1429, Orl√©ans began holding a celebration in honor of the raising of the siege on 8 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2003[httpsbooksgooglecombookside04BDgAAQBAJpgPA209_209]_343-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2003[httpsbooksgooglecombookside04BDgAAQBAJpgPA209_209]-343">[336]</a></sup>
</p><p>After Joan's execution, her role in the Orl√©ans victory encouraged popular support for her rehabilitation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage118_118]_344-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage118_118]-344">[337]</a></sup> Joan became a central part of the annual celebration, and by 1435 a play, <span title="French-language text"><i lang="fr">Mist√®re du si√®ge d'Orl√©ans</i></span> (Mystery of the Siege of Orl√©ans),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin2003[httpsbooksgooglecombookside04BDgAAQBAJpgPA217_217]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage243_243]_345-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin2003[httpsbooksgooglecombookside04BDgAAQBAJpgPA217_217]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage243_243]-345">[338]</a></sup> portrayed her as the vehicle of the divine will that liberated Orl√©ans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHamblin1988[httpsjstororgstable1347436seq3_63‚Äì64]_346-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHamblin1988[httpsjstororgstable1347436seq3_63‚Äì64]-346">[339]</a></sup> The Orl√©ans festival celebrating Joan continues in modern times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOrl√©ans2021PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage242_242‚Äì245]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage192_192]_347-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOrl√©ans2021PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage242_242‚Äì245]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage192_192]-347">[340]</a></sup>
</p><p>Less than a decade after her rehabilitation trial, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_II" title="Pope Pius II">Pope Pius II</a> wrote a brief biography describing her as the maid who saved the kingdom of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage350_350‚Äì352]_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage350_350‚Äì352]-348">[341]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII" title="Louis XII">Louis XII</a> commissioned a full-length biography of her around 1500.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage316_316]RankinQuintal1964[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfirstbiographyof0000rankpage3_3]_349-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage316_316]RankinQuintal1964[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfirstbiographyof0000rankpage3_3]-349">[342]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan's early legacy was closely associated with the <a href="/wiki/Divine_right_of_kings" title="Divine right of kings">divine right</a> of the monarchy to rule France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage56_56]Mackinnon1902[httpsarchiveorgdetailsgrowthdeclineoff00mackuoftpage78_78]Wood1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcrichard0000woodpage150_150]_350-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage56_56]Mackinnon1902[httpsarchiveorgdetailsgrowthdeclineoff00mackuoftpage78_78]Wood1988[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcrichard0000woodpage150_150]-350">[343]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, her reputation came into question because of her association with the monarchy and religion,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage15_15]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage39_39]_351-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage15_15]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage39_39]-351">[344]</a></sup> and the festival in her honor held at Orl√©ans was suspended in 1793.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFrance1909[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles1948819488-h19488-hhtmINTRODUCTION_lix‚Äìlx]_352-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFrance1909[httpswwwgutenbergorgfiles1948819488-h19488-hhtmINTRODUCTION_lix‚Äìlx]-352">[345]</a></sup> In 1803, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleon_Bonaparte" title="Napoleon Bonaparte">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> authorized its renewal<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage256_256]_353-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWarner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage256_256]-353">[346]</a></sup> and the creation of a new statue of Joan at Orl√©ans, stating: "The illustrious Joan¬†... proved that there is no miracle which French genius cannot accomplish when national independence is threatened."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEConner2004[httpsarchiveorgdetailsageofnapoleon0000connpage89_89]Guillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage249_249]_354-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEConner2004[httpsarchiveorgdetailsageofnapoleon0000connpage89_89]Guillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage249_249]-354">[347]</a></sup>
</p><p>Since then, she has become a prominent symbol as the defender of the French nation. After the French defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>, Joan became a rallying point for a new crusade to reclaim Lorraine, the province of her birth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage250_250]Maddox2012[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrETxD8KcnUICpgPA444_444]_355-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage250_250]Maddox2012[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrETxD8KcnUICpgPA444_444]-355">[348]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">Third Republic</a> held a patriotic civic holiday in her honor,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq12_450]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage144_144]_356-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq12_450]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage144_144]-356">[349]</a></sup> on 8 May to celebrate her victory at Orl√©ans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage254_255]Sexsmith1990[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458seq5_129]_357-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage254_255]Sexsmith1990[httpswwwjstororgstable42630458seq5_129]-357">[350]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/French_ship_Jeanne_d%27Arc" title="French ship Jeanne d'Arc">series of French warships</a> have been named for her.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGS2003_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGS2003-358">[351]</a></sup> During World War I, her image was used to inspire victory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq11_449]Gaehtgens2018[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidYgldDwAAQBAJpgPA45_45]_359-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq11_449]Gaehtgens2018[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidYgldDwAAQBAJpgPA45_45]-359">[352]</a></sup> In World War II, all sides of the French cause appealed to her legacy:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA130_130]_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA130_130]-360">[353]</a></sup> she was a symbol for <a href="/wiki/Philippe_P%C3%A9tain" title="Philippe P√©tain">Philippe P√©tain</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq14_452]Cohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA130_130]_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248seq14_452]Cohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA130_130]-361">[354]</a></sup> a model for <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a>'s leadership of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_French" title="Free French">Free French</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA138_138]Dunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA62_62]_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA138_138]Dunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA62_62]-362">[355]</a></sup> and an example for the <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance#Communists" title="French Resistance">Communist resistance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage220_220]_363-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage220_220]-363">[356]</a></sup> More recently, her association with the monarchy and national liberation has made her a symbol for the French far right, including the monarchist movement <a href="/wiki/Action_Fran%C3%A7aise" title="Action Fran√ßaise">Action Fran√ßaise</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA62_62]_364-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA62_62]-364">[357]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Rally" title="National Rally">National Front Party</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGildea1996[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid-JcLOEKvJ2kCpgPA165_165]Margolis1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage265_265]_365-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGildea1996[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid-JcLOEKvJ2kCpgPA165_165]Margolis1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage265_265]-365">[358]</a></sup> Joan's image has been used by the entire spectrum of French politics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248_439]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage3_3]_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrown2012[httpswwwjstororgstable43489248_439]Mock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage3_3]-366">[359]</a></sup> and she is an important reference in political dialogue about French identity and unity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage145_145]_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMock2011[httpsarchiveorgdetailssymbolsofdefeati0000mockpage145_145]-367">[360]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Saint_and_heroic_woman">Saint and heroic woman</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg"><img alt="See caption" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1062" data-file-width="770" decoding="async" height="234" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg/170px-Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg/255px-Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg/340px-Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Albert_Lynch_-_Jeanne_d%27Arc.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illustration by <a href="/wiki/Albert_Lynch" title="Albert Lynch">Albert Lynch</a> (1903, in <i>Figaro Illustr√©</i> magazine)</div></div></div>
<p>Joan is a <a href="/wiki/Saint#Catholic_church" title="Saint">saint</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>. She was viewed as a religious figure in Orl√©ans after the siege was lifted and an annual <a href="/wiki/Panegyric" title="Panegyric">panegyric</a> was pronounced there on her behalf until the 1800s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGildea1996[httpswwwgooglecombookseditionThe_Past_in_French_History-JcLOEKvJ2kChlengbpv1bsqpanegyric_155‚Äì156]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage311_311‚Äì312,_fn_24]_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGildea1996[httpswwwgooglecombookseditionThe_Past_in_French_History-JcLOEKvJ2kChlengbpv1bsqpanegyric_155‚Äì156]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage311_311‚Äì312,_fn_24]-368">[361]</a></sup> In 1849, the Bishop of Orlƒóans <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Dupanloup" title="F√©lix Dupanloup">F√©lix Dupanloup</a> delivered an oration that attracted international attention,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETaylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq223_238]_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETaylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq223_238]-369">[362]</a></sup> and in 1869 petitioned Rome to begin <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">beatification</a> proceedings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGildea1996PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage244_244‚Äì245]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq23_238]_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGildea1996PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage244_244‚Äì245]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq23_238]-370">[363]</a></sup> She was beatified by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_X" title="Pope Pius X">Pope Pius X</a> in 1909, and <a href="/wiki/Canonization_of_Joan_of_Arc" title="Canonization of Joan of Arc">canonized</a> on 16 May 1920 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Benedict_XV" title="Pope Benedict XV">Pope Benedict XV</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage245_245]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq25_240]_371-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage245_245]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq25_240]-371">[364]</a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Calendar_of_saints" title="Calendar of saints">feast day</a> is 30 May, the anniversary of her execution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page244_244]_372-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page244_244]-372">[365]</a></sup> In an <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_letter" title="Ecclesiastical letter">apostolic letter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_XI" title="Pope Pius XI">Pope Pius XI</a> declared Joan one of the patron saints of France on 2 March 1922.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPius_XI1922[httpsarchiveorgdetailssim_acta-apostolicae-sedis_1922-04-03_14_7page187_187]_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPius_XI1922[httpsarchiveorgdetailssim_acta-apostolicae-sedis_1922-04-03_14_7page187_187]-373">[366]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan was canonized as a <a href="/wiki/Virgin_(title)" title="Virgin (title)">Virgin</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage162_162]_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage162_162]-374">[367]</a></sup> not as a <a href="/wiki/Christian_martyr" title="Christian martyr">Christian martyr</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChenu1990[httpsarchiveorgdetailsbookofchristianm00chenpage98_98]Ghezzi1996Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage106_106_fn8]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage264_264]_375-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChenu1990[httpsarchiveorgdetailsbookofchristianm00chenpage98_98]Ghezzi1996Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage106_106_fn8]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage264_264]-375">[368]</a></sup> because she had been put to death by a canonically constituted court,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage256_256]_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage256_256]-376">[369]</a></sup> which did not execute for her faith in Christ,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidF3qFtB-Lq14CpgPA105_105]_377-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2002[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidF3qFtB-Lq14CpgPA105_105]-377">[370]</a></sup> but for her private revelation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]_378-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]-378">[371]</a></sup> Nevertheless, she has been popularly venerated as a martyr since her death:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen360_842]Meltzer2001[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_SEPFzzpvp0CpgPA192_192]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage6_6],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage252_252]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage29_29_fn86]_379-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELowell1896[httpsarchiveorgdetailsJoanOfArc1896pagen360_842]Meltzer2001[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_SEPFzzpvp0CpgPA192_192]Pernoud1955[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage6_6],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsretrialofjoanofa00regipage252_252]Taylor2006[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclapucel00unsepage29_29_fn86]-379">[372]</a></sup> one who suffered for her modesty and purity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage249_249]McInerney2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgrHIDAAAQBAJpgPA210_210]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgrHIDAAAQBAJpgPA211_211]Sullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage30_30‚Äì31]_380-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]Michelet1855[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcmaidofo00michpage249_249]McInerney2003[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgrHIDAAAQBAJpgPA210_210]‚Äì[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidgrHIDAAAQBAJpgPA211_211]Sullivan1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsinterrogationofj00sullpage30_30‚Äì31]-380">[373]</a></sup>
her country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]Guillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage249_249]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage268_268]_381-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage210_210]Guillemin1970[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanmaidoforlean0000guilpage249_249]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage268_268]-381">[374]</a></sup>
and the strength of her convictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChenu1990[httpsarchiveorgdetailsbookofchristianm00chenpage98_98‚Äì99]_382-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChenu1990[httpsarchiveorgdetailsbookofchristianm00chenpage98_98‚Äì99]-382">[375]</a></sup> Joan is also <a href="/wiki/Calendar_of_saints_(Church_of_England)" title="Calendar of saints (Church of England)">remembered as a visionary</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commemoration_(observance)" title="Commemoration (observance)">commemoration</a> on 30 May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_Calendar2021_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_Calendar2021-3">[2]</a></sup> She is revered in the <a href="/wiki/Pantheon_(religion)" title="Pantheon (religion)">pantheon</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cao_Dai" title="Cao Dai">Cao Dai</a> religion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBoal2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintroductiontowo2005unsepage208_208]_383-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBoal2005[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintroductiontowo2005unsepage208_208]-383">[376]</a></sup>
</p><p>While Joan was alive, she was already being compared to biblical women heroes, such as <a href="/wiki/Esther" title="Esther">Esther</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Judith#Main_characters" title="Judith">Judith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Deborah" title="Deborah">Deborah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFraioli1981[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364_811],_[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364seq3_813‚Äì814]_384-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFraioli1981[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364_811],_[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364seq3_813‚Äì814]-384">[377]</a></sup> Her claim of virginity, which signified her virtue and sincerity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage126_126‚Äì127]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage30_30‚Äì31]Meltzer2001[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_SEPFzzpvp0CpgPA94_94]_385-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage126_126‚Äì127]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage30_30‚Äì31]Meltzer2001[httpsbooksgooglecombooksid_SEPFzzpvp0CpgPA94_94]-385">[378]</a></sup> was upheld by women of status from both the Armagnac and Burgundian-English sides of the Hundred Years' War: Yolande of Aragon, Charles's mother-in-law, and <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Burgundy" title="Anne of Burgundy">Anne of Burgundy</a>, Duchess of Bedford.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page97_97],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page168_168]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage54_54],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage154_154]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage30_30‚Äì31],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage105_105]_386-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECastor2015[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page97_97],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarchistory0000cast_n6r7page168_168]Gies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage54_54],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage154_154]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage30_30‚Äì31],_[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage105_105]-386">[379]</a></sup>
</p><p>Joan has been described as a model of an autonomous woman who challenged traditions of masculinity and femininity<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage123_123‚Äì125]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage103_103]_387-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage123_123‚Äì125]Sullivan1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage103_103]-387">[380]</a></sup> to be heard as an individual<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq1_24‚Äì29]_388-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq1_24‚Äì29]-388">[381]</a></sup> in a patriarchal culture<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq1_24‚Äì29]_388-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq1_24‚Äì29]-388">[381]</a></sup>‚Äîsetting her own course by heeding the voices of her visions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage127_127‚Äì129]_389-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcheretic0000barspage127_127‚Äì129]-389">[382]</a></sup>  She fulfilled the traditionally male role of a military leader,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage104_104‚Äì105]Fraioli1981[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364seq7_817]Sproles1996[httpswwwjstororgstable23539706seq5_162]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq2_217]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage216_216]_390-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage104_104‚Äì105]Fraioli1981[httpswwwjstororgstable2847364seq7_817]Sproles1996[httpswwwjstororgstable23539706seq5_162]Taylor2012[httpswwwjstororgstable23240136seq2_217]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage216_216]-390">[383]</a></sup> while maintaining her status as a valiant woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage104_104]_391-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDworkin1987[httpsarchiveorgdetailsintercourse0000dworpage104_104]-391">[384]</a></sup> Merging qualities associated with both genders,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq4_29]_392-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBarstow1985[httpswwwjstororgstable40003571seq4_29]-392">[385]</a></sup> Joan has <a href="/wiki/Cultural_depictions_of_Joan_of_Arc" title="Cultural depictions of Joan of Arc">inspired numerous artistic and cultural works</a> for many centuries. In the nineteenth century, hundreds of work of art about her‚Äîincluding biographies, plays, and musical scores‚Äîwere created in France, and her story became popular as an artistic subject in Europe and North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA38_38]_393-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDunn2021[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidSG4HEAAAQBAJpgPA38_38]-393">[386]</a></sup> By the 1960s, she was the topic of thousands of books.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage16_16‚Äì17]_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELightbody1961[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjudgementsofjoan0000lighpage16_16‚Äì17]-394">[387]</a></sup> Her legacy has become global, and inspires novels, plays, poems, operas, films, paintings, children's books, advertising, computer games, comics and popular culture across the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA110_110]_395-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECohen2014[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidDcfbAgAAQBAJpgPA110_110]-395">[388]</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Her birthday is sometimes given as 6 January. This is based on a letter by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Perceval_de_Boulainvilliers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Perceval de Boulainvilliers (page does not exist)">Perceval de Boulainvilliers</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">¬†[<a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perceval_de_Boulainvilliers" title="fr:Perceval de Boulainvilliers">fr</a>]</span>, a councillor of Charles VII, stating that Joan was born on the <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(holiday)" title="Epiphany (holiday)">feast of the Epiphany</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage6_6]_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage6_6]-13">[12]</a></sup> but his letter is filled with literary <a href="/wiki/Trope_(literature)" title="Trope (literature)">tropes</a> that make it questionable as a statement of fact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage23_23]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage55_55]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage278_278]_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage23_23]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage55_55]Warner1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcimageof0000warnpage278_278]-14">[13]</a></sup> There is no other evidence of her being born on Epiphany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage265_265]_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage265_265]-15">[14]</a></sup></span>

<li id="cite_note-39"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-39">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Fauquembergue's doodle on the margin of a Parliament's register is the only known contemporary representation of Joan. It is an <a href="/wiki/Artist%27s_impression" title="Artist's impression">artist's impression</a> depicting her with long hair and a dress rather than with her hair cut short and in armor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page31_31]Maddox2012[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrETxD8KcnUICpgPA442_442]_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEDeVries1999[httpsarchiveorgdetailsisbn_9780750918053page31_31]Maddox2012[httpsbooksgooglecombooksidrETxD8KcnUICpgPA442_442]-38">[36]</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-62">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The woman in this saying is assumed to refer to Isabeau of Bavaria,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage31_31]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage6_6]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage44_44]_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGies1981[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclegendr0000giespage31_31]Harrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage6_6]Pernoud1962[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcbyherse00pernpage44_44]-60">[57]</a></sup> but this is uncertain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAdams2010[httpswwwgooglecombookseditionThe_Life_and_Afterlife_of_Isabeau_of_BavXlnwD9UTCZYChlengbpv1pgPA47printsecfrontcover_47‚Äì49]Fraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage58_58]_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAdams2010[httpswwwgooglecombookseditionThe_Life_and_Afterlife_of_Isabeau_of_BavXlnwD9UTCZYChlengbpv1pgPA47printsecfrontcover_47‚Äì49]Fraioli2000[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcearlyde0000fraipage58_58]-61">[58]</a></sup></span>

<li id="cite_note-246"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-246">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The details of Joan's abjuration are unclear because the original document, which may have been only eight lines long,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage290_290‚Äì291]_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHarrison2014[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarclifetra0000harrpage290_290‚Äì291]-244">[240]</a></sup> was replaced with a longer one in the official record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage266_266‚Äì267]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage130_130‚Äì131]RankinQuintal1964[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfirstbiographyof0000rankpage113_101]_245-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELucie-Smith1976[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarc0000lucipage266_266‚Äì267]PernoudClin1986[httpsarchiveorgdetailsjoanofarcherstor00pernpage130_130‚Äì131]RankinQuintal1964[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfirstbiographyof0000rankpage113_101]-245">[241]</a></sup> <a href="#CITEREFQuicherat1841a">Quicherat 1841a</a>, pp.¬†<a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/ProcesDeCondamnationV1/page/446" rel="nofollow">446‚Äì448</a> provides the official text of the abjuration document in French. See <a href="#CITEREFLinder2017">Linder 2017</a> for an English translation.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-269"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-269">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the foreground of this allegorical work, Guillaume Bouill√©, who opened the inquest, is handing Joan, who died twenty years previously but is symbolically present, the text of her rehabilitation. The figures in the background are <a href="/wiki/Jean_Br%C3%A9hal" title="Jean Br√©hal">Jean Br√©hal</a> (standing), the inquisitor; <a href="/wiki/Jean_Juv%C3%A9nal_des_Ursins" title="Jean Juv√©nal des Ursins">Jean Juv√©nal des Ursins</a>, archbishop of Reims (enthroned in the center); and one of the other commissioners (enthroned), either <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_Chartier_(bishop)" title="Guillaume Chartier (bishop)">Guillaume Chartier (bishop)</a>, bishop of Paris or <a href="/wiki/Richard_Olivier_de_Longueil" title="Richard Olivier de Longueil">Richard Olivier de Longueil</a>, bishop of Coutances.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELGPC2022_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELGPC2022-268">[263]</a></sup></span>

<li id="cite_note-312"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-312">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> For example, <a href="#CITEREFMackowiak2007">Mackowiak 2007</a>, pp.¬†<a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/postmortemsolvin0000mack/page/138" rel="nofollow">138‚Äì139</a> points out problems with assuming Joan had schizophrenia, ergot poisoning or temporal lobe issues; <a href="#CITEREFHughes2005">Hughes 2005</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://www.epilepsybehavior.com/article/S1525-5050(04)00354-3/fulltext" rel="nofollow">abstract</a> disputes the conjecture that she had epilepsy; <a href="#CITEREFNoresYakovleff1995">Nores &amp; Yakovleff 1995</a>, <a class="external text" href="https://www.karger.com/Article/Abstract/119218" rel="nofollow">abstract</a> argue against her visions being caused by tuberculosis; one of Joan's advocates at the canonization trial pointed out that her case did not meet the clinical descriptions of hysteria;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage222_222]_311-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKelly1996[httpsarchiveorgdetailsfreshverdictsonj0000unsepage222_222]-311">[305]</a></sup> and <a href="#CITEREFRatnasuriya1986">Ratnasuriya 1986</a>, pp.¬†<a class="external text" href="https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/014107688607900413" rel="nofollow">234‚Äì235</a> critiques diagnosing Joan as a creative psychopath.</span>
